Spring and Autumn

A Widow's Heart 232

— Chen Liang

In Liujia Village, with twenty-three households, the one who gets up earliest every morning is Sister-in-law Liu the Second.

Liu the Second died of illness last spring, leaving behind three to five mu of land and a dilapidated cottage. She was young and widowed, without children, without parents-in-law, all alone. She felt that her husband had treated her very well when he was alive, not calling her to do the heavy work in the fields. She simply couldn't bear to remarry. When she was a young girl, she heard people say that a woman who doesn't remarry after her husband dies is remarkable. People, perhaps even the officials in the yamen, would build her a memorial arch, and she would be praised forever.

It's still possible to support the household expenses alone, but that debt, with its monthly interest, felt like a thousand-pound stone pressing down on her, leaving her no days of ease. The debt was incurred when her husband died, from borrowing money to buy a coffin. Of course, she was responsible for repaying it. At this time, there was no other way but to work hard, doing her own field work and then helping other families with their busy work. Indeed, everyone in the village said that Sister-in-law Liu the Second was willing to endure hardship and withstand loneliness.

But after all, she was young, and the physical changes were quite distressing. And there was also—there was also the provocation of the seasons and the outside world. She saw how happy other people's wives were with their husbands, weeding in the same field, eating at the same plank table, resting in the shade of the same tree. As for herself, wherever she went, she dragged a sad, lonely shadow. When she couldn't bear the desolation of widowhood, her heart trembled.

"Am I really so lacking in fortitude?!" She would immediately suppress her trembling heart. The iron wall of morality surrounded her heavily, and it seemed like a tall memorial arch of chastity stood before her, emitting a bitter smile, reminding her of her husband's kindness when he was alive and the faces of many, many stern commentators from the outside world. And so, like a prisoner being watched, she worked, worked desperately, day, month, year—an endless succession of years, an endless lonely and desolate life.

When she saw a rooster chasing a hen around the threshing ground, she felt that the existence of beasts was more carefree and more free than that of people, because they simply didn't have this thing called "reputation."

And yet, Sister-in-law Liu the Second was still climbing towards that glorious memorial arch of chastity, sighing, "Ah, a virtuous widow?"

Modern Women and "Mōdan" Women 233

— Níng Yī

Speaking of "modern," unless you're not a modern friend, it would be strange if anyone said they didn't know! As for "Mōdan"? Perhaps some people don't understand, but it's actually one and the same with "modern," just a Japanese product? ||| "Modern" is translated as "Mōdan" in Japanese. |||

The modern women mentioned here naturally refer to our esteemed country's "misses" and hard-working ladies, while the "Mōdan" women naturally refer to the average Japanese "misses."

Undoubtedly, when it comes to modern women, the typical image in most people's minds is like this: ||| Perhaps this is an arbitrary assumption after being influenced by what they've seen and heard. ||| Their hair is permed, their faces are painted red like a monkey's butt, their qipao (cheongsam) is skin-tight, they wear high heels, their fingers and toes are painted with scarlet nail polish, they walk with a swaying waist, they know how to smile charmingly, chew Wrigley's gum, dance, smoke, and more... As for "Mōdan" women? They also know these tricks, but they walk with a straight posture, and their clothing is even more "Mōdan" than modern women, very few "Mōdan" women wear wooden clogs or kimonos, most are dressed in Western suits, completely Westernized, with no "Mōdan" air at all? But modern women? They still refuse to give up the qipao, to achieve the goal of complete Westernization? The result is like learning science from others, only getting a superficial understanding. One more point is worth noting, and it's the biggest difference: "Mōdan" women are completely Westernized, but their clothing material is domestic, while modern women refuse to give up the qipao, but their clothing material is always imported. The difference between modern women and "Mōdan" women lies in this, which is also the reason why "Mōdan" women are more valuable?

Women's Liberation and Not Wearing Underpants 234

— Miào Shén

Before women cut their hair, people advocated cutting hair, thinking that it could save expenses and time. But what is the result now? After cutting their hair, there's one more thing to do: perming it. Each electric perm costs six yuan, and a water perm costs ten yuan. The time spent is more than two or three hours, which is more expensive and more time-consuming than before. Who would have expected this?

Recently, there's also a trend of women going barefoot with bare legs. Their reason is: it's cool and comfortable, and it can also save a pair of socks, seemingly planning from an economic perspective again. Little do they know that some women apply white and fragrant Parisian powder on their legs, and paint their toes with bright rose-colored nail polish. This cost is much more expensive than a pair of socks. Obviously, it's gradually deviating from the original purpose of advocating, who would have expected this?

Recently, some people have advocated abolishing women's trousers (kù), replacing them with skirts. The reason is naturally similar to going barefoot with bare legs. In addition to that, there's another reason: it's said to reduce the mystery of women. For example, Japanese women don't often wear trousers, and their relationships between men and women are calm, and the issue of sex is not particularly indulgent. Western countries, such as French women, also don't wear trousers, only wearing Maillot, and they don't have any drawbacks. I believe that after a few more years, Chinese women will definitely not wear trousers either, truly returning to nature. As for the result, the consumption of makeup will be even more alarming!

For many years, has the result of the women's movement only been seeking the liberation of clothing and the liberation of sex? It's truly quite strange!

Loving Daughter's Flesh 235

— Huàn Bīng

Old Man Chen couldn't sleep all night, thinking as much as he could.

Sometimes lying horizontally on the bed, sometimes taking puffs of his water pipe, slapping the banana leaf fan loudly in the mosquito net.

These past few years, he didn't know what bad luck he had encountered. Ever since he managed to get a lucrative position, he was quite powerful, with runners and servants working for him. Later, not long after, the government laid off staff, tax collection duty was prosperous and didn't bear great risks, so apart from this, he simply didn't want to condescend to any other work. However, sitting idle and consuming resources, how could he sustain it for three to five years with a little savings? It had long been pawned away. His old wife also died the year before, which made him feel even more pain. Fortunately, Heaven never cuts off all paths, his daughter was growing up, originally belonging to someone else's family, not expecting her to do anything. Now, he was entirely relying on her flesh to support him.

In his wild thoughts, it seemed that his conscience was severely condemned, but after a while, he acted as if nothing had happened. He heard that the daughter's room next door was silent, without any sound. ||| In fact, the door was still bolted shut from the inside, he knew, and he understood everything. But, where did the money for his effortless meals, his few puffs of smoke, and a few games of cards come from?

X X X X X X X X

In the hazy morning mist, she swayed at the entrance of a hotel with a pale and exhausted face. Not long after, she hired a rickshaw, and turning along a city wall, S City wasn't very big, and her home wasn't far from the city.

Her father—Old Man Chen, was sound asleep, so she slipped into the gate without anyone knowing. The birds resting in the courtyard hadn't flown away yet, she couldn't care about anything, hastily opened her room door and went in, took off the gauze qipao outside, turned over, fell on the bed, forgetting all the pain.

It was already late morning, she woke up from her daze. The day's tasks, washing clothes, cooking, everything was waiting for her alone to take on!

Suddenly, she seemed to have lost something. Clearly, just now, she herself, because she was too tired, had casually put a five-yuan bill on the table, but it had disappeared!

Examination and Recruitment of Female Staff 236

— Zǐ Yún

The news that a certain large company was recruiting female staff spread quickly. In less than a week, it had received nearly three hundred applications, each application accompanied by a four-inch half-body photo and a letter. However, the company only needed to hire twenty-three people, and even with alternates, it would never be able to recruit more than fifty people. Moreover, at that time, eleven people had already been internally decided upon, introduced by directors and senior staff. So in reality, there were only twelve slots available.

There were only twelve slots, but there were nearly three hundred applications. Therefore, the examination committee, jointly organized by the three heads of the procurement department, personnel department, and accounting department, along with the assistant manager, first eliminated nearly two hundred applications from the nearly three hundred applications based on the beauty of the faces in the photos. Leaving one hundred applications, notifying them to come to the company for an interview on the morning of a certain day.

On the morning of that day, more than seventy people came one after another. The examination committee was set up in the assistant manager's office. The assistant manager sat at the desk. The three heads sat on the sofa against the wall. The female applicants were led into the assistant manager's office one by one by the teaboy, and were personally questioned by the assistant manager. The three heads each scored them. The scoring criteria were divided into four items: "Beauty," "Attitude," "Speech," and "Patience." After the exam, the average score of the three was calculated to determine whether to keep or eliminate them. As a result, twelve regular employees and twenty-three alternates were selected. However, it was announced to the public that there were twenty-three regular employees and twenty-three alternates. As for the salary, it was seventeen yuan per month, with one lunch provided by the company every day.

Visiting the Former Residence of Palace Maid Fei 237

— Shā Jīn

When mentioning Palace Maid Fei, people will feel very unfamiliar and indifferent. If I want to make you understand and be moved, then I have to start with her own history.

However, having said that, if I were to simply open the "Biography of Zhen'e" written by predecessors and copy it again, risking the crime of copying someone else's article, the length of the text would also exhaust your interest.

I'll just give you a hint here.

Have you heard of "Dr. Mei's" "Assassinating the Tiger?" If you nod and say yes, then you already understand her enough. She was a martyr who assassinated a bandit chief in the late Ming Dynasty to protect her chastity.

Once, on a snowy dusk, I and several people went to a residence in the Japanese Concession, pulling friends, stepping on the snow, and walked past the Temple of Confucius in the old city of Tianjin. Originally, it wasn't the concession area, but we had arrived in the so-called city. Our route originally followed Asahi Street and went straight to East Ma Road.

The architecture of the Temple of Confucius was still antique, as if it was sleeping soundly in this city. The evening mist gently shrouded it, like weaving its dream shadow. Looking from a distance, there was a tall building on the south side, seemingly very solemn and majestic. We were eager to see it clearly, and walked with slippery steps.

Having taken not a few steps, Jian Bo jumped up as if surprised and said:

"It's here!"

We thought he had found his love, as he had been heartbroken. Everyone asked him in unison:

"Where is it?"

He smiled and pointed to a small archway at the entrance of an alley next to the road. We took a look, and it turned out to be written on it:

"Former Residence of Palace Maid Fei of the Ming Dynasty."

It was written by Yan Xiu of Tianjin. The five large characters had a very thick and majestic style.

Several people, disregarding the muddy snow, jumped into the small alley, wanting to inquire and understand. The first person we encountered was a child selling pancakes; he said he didn't know. Then, we asked a middle-aged man who looked like a gentleman, and he said, "I just arrived too." Later, we met a very old man, and he said very sincerely:

"This place exists, but the house is already occupied by another family. The years are long, and the original ruins have been buried. Even if you could find it with great effort, there's nothing to see."

Our visit was thus interrupted. However, our interest was not exhausted. It wasn't until we saw clearly that the building in the distance was the Drum Tower of the old city of Tianjin that we came back.

After eating dinner, I immediately wrote in my diary:

"The former residence of Fei, a guest in Tianjin, is a few steps from the side of the Temple of Confucius, north of the Drum Tower."

It happened to be seen by Mr. Ding, and he said with a smile:

"This place, Mei Xiaoshu of Tianjin, calls it 'Fei Family Lane.' He also wrote two short poems on the portrait of the palace maid:

The history is vague, but the blood is fresh, A sword of righteousness lasts for a thousand years;

Still there is Qin Liangyu to fight alongside, Killing bandits and serving the king with her beauty.

A loyal heart like a mirror is hard to measure, Leaving behind only pity for the condensed tears;

It should transform into the snow of the Western Mountains, Cold light often shines on the Thirteen Tombs.

Although the poems are old-fashioned, they are still related to literature, why don't you copy them down as well?"

Suffering from High Heels 238

— (Yángzǐjiāng)

Time: 9:15 AM on August 15th of the 23rd year. (Using the grandstand clock as a standard.)

Location: Tram stop at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Ma Huo Road.

People: A young woman around twenty years old, with powder, rouge, a goose-yellow silk qipao, permed hair, high heels, a so-called modern woman.

What happened: The tram arrived at the station, and I was the first to get off. That young woman followed me off, but she didn't hold onto the copper pole, and her foot stepped down. Her right foot didn't stand firmly, and her left foot didn't jump down together.

The high heel of her right foot came off, throwing it out about three to five feet, and the young woman fell down slowly. I wanted to turn around and help her, but the tram driver had already started to help her up. The young woman was very ashamed and angry, and limped to the sidewalk to call for a rickshaw, which shows that she was in pain from the fall. Her face was red and white, a mixture of anger, shame, and fear!

Personal thoughts: The wearing of high heels by modern women has long been criticized by informed people. But criticism is criticism, wearing is wearing, I wonder if they will realize it after seeing my chronicle? (Yángzǐjiāng)

Emerald Melon Small Record 239

— (Qī Fèng Lóu Zhǔ)

Yesterday, I read Mr. Shěn Qín's "Watermelon Lantern Essay" in this publication, which mentioned that Emperor Tongzhi had a watermelon lantern competition on a summer night, and a lotus concubine presented a lantern

, engraved with "Xiāoxiāng Hall Spring Slumber and Secluded Feelings Picture." Tongzhi was overjoyed when he saw it and rewarded her with a natural emerald watermelon, and said; "This is a famous treasure, I wonder if it still exists? Perhaps it was taken away when the Eight-Nation Alliance attacked?" and so on; I suddenly recalled that a few years ago, when the Eastern Tombs were excavated, many treasures were discovered. Four emerald watermelons were stolen from Empress Dowager Cixi's tomb, crystal clear and rounded, completely green, two were darker, called glass green, and two were slightly lighter, named plum blossom green, the value of which was unparalleled. Some say that it was contributed by the Western Regions during the Yuan Dynasty, but it's hard to verify after many years. Since these treasures have recently appeared, it's undoubtedly taken away by the Eight-Nation Alliance. However, according to rumors, these four melons were indeed secretly transported to England by a certain jewelry tycoon and sold at a high price. In recent years, Chinese treasures have flown overseas, I don't know how many, which is very regrettable.

Finance 240

Raw Gold Soars, Sterling Surprisingly Strong

Gold Standard Plunges by Nine Yuan Two

The gold market was affected by the surprise rise of raw gold and the sudden loosening of the British exchange rate. The potential trend in the afternoon is still weak.

Goods Merged into Gold Exchange 241

To be Implemented from October

The issue of merging the gold and goods exchanges has been delayed for a long time and has not been resolved. According to recent confirmed information, all issues have been fully resolved by the representatives of the two exchanges on Wednesday and several conditions have been signed. Therefore, the gold standard part of the goods exchange is about to be merged into the gold exchange. Now, a public notice from the brokerage association is recorded as follows:

"According to the notice from our office, the business rights of the gold and silver parts of our office have been merged with the Shanghai Gold Exchange. The gold standard buying and selling in our office will be suspended at the end of September. New transactions will be stopped from September 15th, and swaps will no longer be held. Special announcement."

Particularly Heavy Month-End Settlements 243

||| Overnight call loan interest rates eased, falling by five points |||

Yesterday was the last day of the month. The silver dollar market conditions were generally unchanged, but call loan rates added water, falling by five points due to ample overnight funds, resulting in a three-point market fluctuation. The market price for silver dollar call loans remained at one dime in the morning and afternoon. However, due to the month-end settlements and Chinese merchants settling out three to four million in silver dollars for rice and other commodities, settlements were particularly heavy. Call loan transactions in the morning reached over 3.4 million for transfers and over 400,000 for new transactions. Afternoon transactions exceeded 500,000, and transactions at the small general meeting exceeded 300,000. Silver dollar pawn loan transactions redeemed over 1.5 million and made new loans of over 3 million. Bank settlements included over 4.0 million in ticket amounts from foreign banks, over 6.8 million in settlements for various commodity exchange pawn loans and miscellaneous loans, over 4.0 million in settlements for account closures, over 600,000 in telegraphic transfer funds, over 2.5 million in foreign exchange settlements, and 1.2 million in warehouse entries. Chinese bank settlements included over 4.9 million in ticket amounts, over 7.2 million in settlements for various commodity exchange pawn loans, miscellaneous taxes, and other loans, over 3.5 million in settlements for account closures, over 700,000 in telegraphic transfer funds, over 1.4 million in foreign exchange settlements, and 800,000 in warehouse exits. Japanese bank settlements included over 3.4 million in ticket amounts, over 5.8 million in settlements for various commodity exchange pawn loans and miscellaneous loans, over 2.2 million in settlements for account closures, over 4.2 million in foreign exchange settlements, and 700,000 in warehouse exits. Native banks settled over 7.5 million in silver dollar public notes, over 1.1 million in silver dollar call loans, redeemed and issued over 2.0 million in banknotes, received over 400,000 in cash, remitted over 1.2 million in various remittance funds, sourced 400,000 from customer routes, cleared 350,000, and settled over 4.0 million in public bonds. Additionally, the total exchange amount at the clearinghouse on the 31st was 15,997,416.43 silver dollars, including 6,367,233.62 silver dollars and 9,630,182.81 silver dollars in exchange transfers.

All-Month Call Loan Interest Rates Set New Record 244

Since the financial community switched to using silver dollar call loans, silver dollar positions have generally been loose due to market conditions, resulting in very few major changes throughout the year. Even the total amount calculated at the end of each month rarely exceeded two yuan, and deposit interest rates did not exceed this level either. This August's silver dollar call loan rates started with a flat first half of the month, but suddenly tightened in the second half, especially on the 24th, reaching a high of 1.5 dimes. As a result, the total interest for the entire month was 2.69 yuan. Averaging over 31 days, this equates to 8.645 cents per day. As a result, the Money Trade Association's regular meeting held for two days set a new record for deposit interest rates of approximately 2.5 yuan.

Yarn and Cotton 247

Cotton Yarn Initially Fell, Then Slightly Recovered

The cotton yarn market initially fell, then rose, showing a slightly calmer trend. The recent decline had been too sharp, falling by more than ten yuan from its peak. This prompted profit-takers to cover their positions, causing the market to rebound. At the same time, sales of spot yarn were higher than yesterday. However, most market sentiment still leaned towards selling short, as the inventory in warehouses was difficult to empty. Nevertheless, the cotton market was still strong, so the yarn market might become slightly stronger.

The cotton yarn market opened lower in the morning due to another decline in U.S. cotton, causing market sentiment to become more uncertain. Cotton Futures Saw Short-Covering Activity in the Afternoon 250

The cotton market fell in the morning and rose in the afternoon, showing a fairly strong trend. However, foreign cotton tended to fall. September Zheng Cotton Recovered by Five Points 251

The cotton market opened lower in the morning, following foreign cotton and the yarn market. Market sentiment was exhausted, and all months fell by three cents. When trading resumed in the afternoon, the market changed suddenly, with prices rising in every session. The reason for this was said to be the irregular climate, with clouds in the sky, raising fears of prolonged rain. Currently, cotton is in the process of opening up. Another report stated that it had been raining in Shandong for a week, and there was flooding in Tongzhou. All these news were favorable to long positions. As a result, buyers and short-covering investors gathered together, causing the market to rebound significantly. Grains: August Flour and Wheat 255

Large Delivery Quantities

Flour reaches 24,000 bags and 63 cars

Yesterday was the delivery date for August flour futures. The total number of contracts actually fulfilled at the exchange for the entire day reached 224,000 bags, including 177,000 bags of Battleship flour and 47,000 bags of Battery flour. It was reported that off-exchange deliveries also reached over 100,000 bags. It was heard that most of the recipients were hedgers from the banking industry. Only over 10,000 bags were delivered to this street, and there was no news of deliveries to out-of-town customers. The ample supply from the factories and the clear sales volume indicate that the future outlook may be continuously weak.

Yesterday's statistics for the delivery of August wheat futures showed an increasing quantity. Since the factories had been sluggish, customers could no longer reject the goods, so the number of deliveries to the exchange also surged. Free Talk

A Playful Discourse 257

— Hui

Theories in the world are sometimes odd, sometimes even; sometimes opposing, sometimes supporting; some are singular, others plural. If the concept of something cannot tolerate concepts beyond itself, then positivity can be relative, opposing, stimulating, and complementary. Otherwise, there will be chaos, contradiction, inability to affirm oneself, and even less to affirm others.

Those with broad knowledge and experience, having many perspectives, are most likely to fall into this chaotic state. Just like solving an extremely complex mathematical problem, a moment of carelessness leads to more and more divergence and confusion. And what about those who are unwilling to think? They often err in the most superficial reasoning, being controlled by a few words, unwilling or unaccustomed to thinking.

Holding this view and looking at various theories today, it is truly a demon-revealing mirror showing their true forms. For example, if you say that Western-style houses are good because they have good lighting and air circulation, the ordinary response can be divided into several types. One is that China also has good houses, therefore Western-style houses are not good. Second, living in Western-style houses is for the wealthy, the wealthy are not good, so Western-style houses are not good. Third, there are too few Western-style houses, and 99% or more of people in China do not live in Western-style houses, so we should not live in Western-style houses, therefore Western-style houses are not good. Fourth, ancient Chinese people did not live in Western-style houses and were still healthy, therefore Western-style houses are not good. ||| This is one example.

This is because the respondent is not thinking, or deliberately saying things.

Another example is that Nietzsche's Superman is merely Nietzsche's thought. But it is said that "if the greatness is only personal," then "there is no use whatsoever." Why? Because "even if there were a hundred Nietzsches, they could not build even one percent of a pyramid in Egypt." Why Nietzsche should be punished to move stones in Egypt to build pyramids is something only a Chinese thinker could imagine. That greatness must have a use is also one of the odd theories. How is it that "personal greatness" has no "use"? It truly belongs to the "chapter of odd theories" ||| This is another example.

Again, it is not thinking, or deliberately saying things.

Ordinary people are easily dazzled by a few people who are willing to think but also have other purposes, because

Summer Nights at Da Chun Bridge 258

— Lan Ru

Because of the quiet outside the city, and to make it easier to read and write, I moved to Da Chun Bridge, the headquarters of this impoverished area.

Those who have lived in Changsha for a long time almost all know that although Da Chun Bridge is too far from the city and inconvenient for transportation, it is Changsha's only "concession." In 1929, when the Red Army entered the city, all places suffered some losses, but Da Chun Bridge was safe and sound. In terms of terrain, Da Chun Bridge really couldn't be better! It is surrounded by mountains on three sides, and the Xiang River runs across the front; a few dozen steps further and you're in the idyllic countryside. I heard that ten years ago, this was still a desolate graveyard, with a small stream flowing into the Xiang River, and a stone bridge across the stream, which is Da Chun Bridge.

Since wealthy people built houses here, more and more people have come to build thatched huts. Now, the residents of Da Chun Bridge, besides two-tenths being wealthy and two-tenths being small merchants, the rest are all poor people who don't even have a foothold.

We initially thought that a sparsely populated place would have fresh air, but here, it's an exception. The Changping Railway is right behind the house, and every day you can hear the train, sounding like a ghost wailing, passing by five times, bringing with it a sky full of black smoke. If at that time you carelessly look up, you will immediately shout, because coal ash has come to visit you.

Suffering all day from the whistle sound and coal ash smoke is not enough, we also have to endure the pushing wheelbarrows, which constantly send a lot of dust in through the window with their constant "ji jie, ji jie" sounds. Like the weather when a strong wind blows in the north, if you don't wipe it for an hour, the dust on the table will be at least three-tenths of an inch thick; if you continue to sit still for two hours, the dust will turn you into an old man with white hair and a yellow-faced actor.

There are even more annoying things: a group of young hooligans play ball outside the window during the day,

and throw small stones in for no reason at night. Although we caught a hooligan ringleader and sent him to the police station the day before yesterday, and had two days of quiet, who knows if he will come back with a vengeance after being released?

Several friends have advised us to move, but when I think about the real advantages of Da Chun Bridge, I don't want to move again.

Two houses past ours live two blind fortune-tellers, three children who pick up coal cinders, Fu Yazi who sells sesame candy on a cart, Wang Er who sets up a stall selling salvaged goods, midwife Fu Saozi, rickshaw puller Si Mazi, a group of refugees who have just fled from the countryside, and several beggars who are cursed and scolded every day and have no names. Some of them sleep with pigs, separated only by a few bamboo fences; some have more than ten family members living in a small thatched hut that is less than ten feet across; some have nothing at all, only a broken bowl in their hands, begging in the streets and alleys during the day, and randomly collapsing in some corner of a public toilet at night, sleeping until dawn.

If you are not afraid of the smell, dirt, or heat, you can run to their thatched huts every night to chat, and I guarantee you will gain unlimited new knowledge. For example, Tan, who just fled from Xinhua the day before yesterday, will tell you how dry the countryside is, and how many farmers are starving to death and committing suicide, which is horrifying. He said, "These people die like dogs, rolled in broken mats, and thrown into earthen pits." He also said, "In the past, when farmers faced famine years, they only knew to starve to death with empty stomachs. Now, they know how to organize into teams to go to the houses of those who have grain to eat row by row." (Note)

Si Mazi, the rickshaw puller, will also tell you how the police oppress the poor and act as running dogs for the wealthy. When a car comes, if the rickshaw stops even a little too slowly, they will immediately beat you half to death with a stick. "Damn it, one time I saw only a driver in the car, and the police saluted him at attention. Haha, damn bootlicker!"

In addition, there are Fu Yazi, Liu the blind man, etc. They will each tell you many different stories, which are all the best materials for your writing.

Walking past Da Chun Bridge, less than a hundred steps away, this area of ​​Meifengming Garden, XX Garden, are all places where coffins are temporarily stored. Sometimes, you can see thousands of people sending off coffins every day, blowing and beating, carried from the city (naturally, these are important people or wives/grandmothers of important people, etc.). As long as you're not blind, everyone wants to run over and watch the excitement: but when they come back, they curse,

"Damn it, so extravagant, where did the money come from?"

At night, on the dark road (there used to be a street lamp, but it broke long ago), many men and children are lying across and lengthwise, wearing only a pair of torn pants. If wealthy gentlemen and ladies come back from the theater in the middle of the night and kick Wang Er's head or step on Fu Yazi's foot, they will definitely curse loudly: "Good dogs don't block the road, these uneducated animals, they deserve to die!"

This curse sometimes wakes you up from a good dream.

Da Chun Bridge, this is Da Chun Bridge's summer night.

"Note" Groups of farmers go to the landlord's house to eat when there is a drought. After eating at one house, they go to another. This is called eating row by row, or just eating in rows.

Extracurricular Talks 259

— Hua Yu

(7) Illiterate Writers

The summary of ancient words written in such difficult characters, we used to call "wen," and now the more modern ones call it "wenxue." This wasn't cut from "wenxue, Ziyou, Zixia," but was imported from Japan, their translation for the English word "Literature." Those who can write such "wen," and now can also write in vernacular, are called "wenxuejia," or "zuojia."

The primary condition for the existence of literature is the ability to write characters. Therefore, there certainly cannot be any "wenxuejia" among the illiterate masses. However, "jia" can exist. Don't laugh at me too soon, I still have something to say. I think that humanity had creation before it had writing. It's just a pity that no one recorded it, and there was no way to record it. Our ancestors, the primitive people, couldn't even speak. In order to work together, they needed to express their opinions, so they gradually developed complex sounds. If everyone was carrying wood and felt it was difficult, but couldn't think of how to express it, and then one person said "Hang yu, hang yu," then that is creation; everyone should admire and apply it, and that would be equivalent to publication; if some mark was used to preserve it, then that would be literature; that person would of course be a writer, and also a "wenxuejia," the "Hang yu Hang pai." Don't laugh, this work is indeed very childish, but the ancients were inferior to people today in many ways, and this is one of them. Even the "Guan guan jujiu, in the river island, graceful lady, a good match for the gentleman" from the Zhou dynasty—it's the first poem in the "Classic of Poetry," so we're so scared that we can only kowtow in admiration. If there hadn't been such a poem before, and a modern poet used this idea to write a vernacular poem and tried to submit it to some supplement, I think nine out of ten times it would be stuffed into the wastepaper basket by the editor. "A pretty good lady, is a good match for the young master!" What is that?

Many of the things in the "Guofeng" section of the "Classic of Poetry" are also the works of illiterate anonymous people. Because they were relatively excellent, everyone passed them on by word of mouth. The royal officials took them out and recorded them because they could be used as administrative references. How many others were eliminated, we don't know. The two great epics of the Greek Homer—let's assume there was such a person—were also originally recited orally; what exists now is someone else's record. The "Zi Ye Ge" and "Du Qu Ge" of the Eastern Jin to Qi Chen dynasties, and the "Zhu Zhi Ci" and "Liu Zhi Ci" of the Tang dynasty, were all originally created by anonymous people, and passed down after being recorded and embellished by literati. This embellishment, while allowing them to be passed down, unfortunately certainly lost much of their original appearance. Now, there are folk songs, mountain songs, fishermen's songs, etc. everywhere, and these are the works of illiterate poets; and there are fairy tales and stories being told, and these are the works of illiterate novelists: they are all illiterate writers.

However, because there is nothing to record the works, they are easily lost, and the scope of circulation cannot be very wide, so very few people know about them. Occasionally, a little is seen by literati, who are often surprised and absorb it into their own works, as new nourishment.

When old literature declines, a new transformation often arises by absorbing folk literature or foreign literature. This example is commonly seen in literary history. Illiterate writers, while not as refined as literati, are robust and fresh.

For such works to be shared by everyone, the writer must first be able to write, and at the same time, readers must be able to read and even write. In a word: give writing to everyone.

Giving Out Gruel 261

— TK

Younger Brother (6) 262

— Zhou Wen

Who knew that the day before I was supposed to set off, after Mom had chosen a good day for me to leave, Wang Er's mother came to ask if we had seen her Wang Er. Only then did Mom realize that her younger brother was not around, and she became anxious. So everyone went out to look for him separately. Mom went to check the cabinets, and everything was fine; the money was also fine; nothing else had been touched at all. Only then did Mom start crying, holding the sweaty clothes that my younger brother had just changed out of yesterday. She cried that she shouldn't have forgotten about his schooling; she hadn't taken good care of him; she hadn't even sewn him a good piece of clothing; and if he was going to leave, he didn't even choose a good day, and left without taking a single penny!

"How can I be worthy of him!" Mom cried like that.

Later, in desperation, Mom could only hope that he had gone to relatives' place. She carefully selected many of his clothes, packed them in my suitcase, and even specially took out a biscuit tin that my younger brother usually loved and filled it with some sugar-fried rice puffs. "When you see your younger brother, say, 'Here, this is for him, tell him not to forget Mom...'"

Mom choked up and cried as she said this, tears dripping into the rice puff tin.

"How can I finish thinking about it! When you hadn't come home yet, he said, 'Mom, you've worked hard, I'll watch the store next year.' I said, ... And he said, 'Mom, don't make clothes for me anymore, I can still wear my older brother's...' How could I know that he was just deceiving me to leave! He threw away so many thoughts, how can I..."

Mom couldn't continue speaking as tears welled up again. I was truly ashamed, standing helplessly beside her.

"Mom, Younger Brother won't get lost, he must have gone there. I don't want to take a sedan chair anymore. I'll walk too."

Mom suddenly opened her eyes wide and looked at me, her lips trembling with emotion.

"No," she said. "The sedan chair has already been booked, take it, don't let people laugh at you! Still take the sedan chair, Mom can eat congee if it's okay. As long as you do well outside, rise higher and higher every day, and earn money to come back. You just need to remember to tell Younger Brother, don't forget Mom..."

I sat in the sedan chair and left my hometown amidst many envious glances. When I arrived at my relatives' place, they indeed said that my younger brother was already there. They originally said they would call him back right away, but he refused no matter what. He said he could even work as a stoker. So they had no choice but to leave him here as a soldier.

On the day I arrived, I really wanted to see him right away, but he wouldn't come no matter what. It wasn't until the third day that I saw him rushing happily towards me at the entrance of the secretariat. I almost didn't recognize him. He had already changed into a gray cloth military uniform, with a small white identification tag hanging on it. This change in him made me feel a bit of subtle pain in my heart. Thinking about our differences, I felt very uneasy. I was just about to greet him, but he turned around and ran out. After that, although we met, it was only a few words, without any good news...
